<tr>
<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Indo-European_topics" title="Template:Indo-European topics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Indo-European_topics" title="Template talk:Indo-European topics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Indo-European_topics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Romani</b> (also spelled <b>Romany</b>; <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="/-/ affix">-</span></span>/</a></span></span>), or <b>Roma</b>, are a traditionally <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> ethnic group, living mostly <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">in Europe</a> and the Americas and originating from the <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">northern</a> regions of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock2002.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2F.3Fid.3DMG0ahVw-kdwC.26lpg.3DPP1.26pg.3DPR20__xx.5D_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock2002.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2F.3Fid.3DMG0ahVw-kdwC.26lpg.3DPP1.26pg.3DPR20_xx.5D-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GoldbergBennahum2015_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoldbergBennahum2015-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BroughtonEllingham1999_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BroughtonEllingham1999-54">[54]</a></sup> presumably from where the states <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haryana" title="Haryana">Haryana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_India" title="Punjab, India">Punjab</a> exist today.<sup id="cite_ref-GoldbergBennahum2015_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoldbergBennahum2015-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BroughtonEllingham1999_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BroughtonEllingham1999-54">[54]</a></sup> The Romani are widely known among English-speaking people by the <a href="/wiki/Exonym_and_endonym" title="Exonym and endonym">exonym</a> "<b>Gypsies</b>" (or "<i>Gipsies</i>"), which some people consider pejorative due to its connotations of illegality and irregularity.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Romani are <a href="/wiki/Romani_diaspora" title="Romani diaspora">dispersed</a>, with their concentrated populations in Europe&#160;–  especially <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> including <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_France" title="Southern France">Southern France</a>. They originated in <a href="/wiki/Northern_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern India">Northern India</a> and arrived in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Mid-West Asia</a>, then Europe, around 1,000 years ago,<sup id="cite_ref-kenrick_intro_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenrick_intro-56">[56]</a></sup> either separating from the <a href="/wiki/Dom_people" title="Dom people">Dom people</a> or, at least, having a similar history;<sup id="cite_ref-Domari_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Domari-57">[57]</a></sup> the ancestors of both the Romani and the Dom left North India sometime between the sixth and eleventh century.<sup id="cite_ref-kenrick_intro_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenrick_intro-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the 19th century, some Romani have also migrated to the Americas. There are an estimated one million <a href="/wiki/Roma_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma in the United States">Roma in the United States</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-time_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-6">[6]</a></sup> and 800,000 in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, most of whose ancestors emigrated in the nineteenth century from eastern Europe. Brazil also includes some Romani descended from people deported by the government of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Inquisition" title="Inquisition">Inquisition</a> in the colonial era.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In migrations since the late nineteenth century, Romani have also moved to other countries in South America and to Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESutherland1986_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESutherland1986-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In February 2016, during the International Roma Conference, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_External_Affairs_(India)" title="Minister of External Affairs (India)">Indian Minister of External Affairs</a> stated that the people of the Roma community were children of India. The conference ended with a recommendation to the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> to recognize the Roma community spread across 30 countries as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_diaspora" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian diaspora">Indian diaspora</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-diaspora_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a> is divided into several <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a>, which add up to an estimated number of speakers larger than two million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatras2002239_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatras2002239-61">[61]</a></sup> The total number of Romani people is at least twice as large (several times as large according to high estimates). Many Romani are native speakers of the language current in their country of residence, or of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_language" title="Mixed language">mixed languages</a> combining the two; those <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">varieties</a> are sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Para-Romani" title="Para-Romani">Para-Romani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Romani_people" title="Names of the Romani people">Names of the Romani people</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exonyms">Exonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Exonyms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> <i>bohème</i>, <i>bohémien</i>, from the Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, whence they came, carrying <a href="/wiki/Letters_patent" title="Letters patent">writs of protection</a> from King <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Sigismund of Bohemia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-schade_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schade-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> <i>gitan</i>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> <i>gypsy</i>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> <i>gitano</i>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> <i>kipti</i>, all from <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <span lang="gr">Αἰγύπτιος</span> <i>Aigýptios</i> "Egyptian" (corrupted form: <span lang="gr">Γύφτος</span> <i>Gýphtos</i>), and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a> <i>faraonépe</i> from Greek <span lang="gr">φαραώ</span> <i>pharaó</i> "pharaoh" – referring to their allegedly Egyptian provenance.<sup id="cite_ref-schade_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schade-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> <i>tzigane</i> (for Hungarian gypsies), <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> <i>tzigane</i>, <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old High German language">Old High German</a> <i>zigeuner</i>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> <i>zigeuner</i>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> <i>zigeuner</i>,<a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Church Slavic language">Old Church Slavic</a> ациганинъ, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> <i>zingaro</i>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a> <i>țigan</i>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a> <i>cigány</i>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a> "cikán", <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> <i>cigano</i>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> <i>çingene</i>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a> <i>cigán</i> or <i>cigáň</i>, <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian</a> <i>singano</i>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> <i>цыгане</i>, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a> <i>ციგანი</i>; from <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <span lang="gr">ἀθίγγανος</span> <i>athínganos</i> (corrupted form: <span lang="gr">τσιγγάνος</span> <i>tsingános</i>), "<a href="/wiki/Untouchability" title="Untouchability">untouchable</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-schade_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schade-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Nawar_(people)" title="Nawar (people)">Nawar</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Zott" title="Zott">Zott</a></i>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Endonyms">Endonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Endonyms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a> Rom "man", if not from <a href="/wiki/Coptic_language" title="Coptic language">Coptic</a> ⲣⲱⲙⲉ, "man", is <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a> रॊम (roma) "the city Rome", probably from <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <span lang="gr">Ῥωμαῖος</span> <i>Rhomaíos</i> "Roman", <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Greeks" title="Names of the Greeks">signifying</a> Greeks or <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BBm" title="Rûm">more general</a> inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a>, who considered themselves successors of Ancient Rome. The <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a> word for "man" मनुष (manusha) is related to <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> Mensch and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> man.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a> सिनधु (sindhu) is a river or stream of water in general. In particular, it denotes the river <a href="/wiki/Indus" class="mw-redirect" title="Indus">Indus</a> and the country around it (commonly called <a href="/wiki/Sindh" title="Sindh">Sindh</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romani_usage">Romani usage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Romani usage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a>, <i>Rom</i> is a masculine noun, meaning 'man of the Roma ethnic group' or 'man, husband', with the plural <i>Roma</i>. The feminine of <i>Rom</i> in the Romani language is <i>Romni</i>. However, in most cases, in other languages <i>Rom</i> is now used for people of all genders.<sup id="cite_ref-words_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-words-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Romani</i> is the feminine adjective, while <i>Romano</i> is the masculine adjective. Some Romanies use <i>Rom</i> or <i>Roma</i> as an ethnic name, while others (such as the <a href="/wiki/Sinti" title="Sinti">Sinti</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Romanichal" title="Romanichal">Romanichal</a>) do not use this term as a self-ascription for the entire ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock2002xix_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock2002xix-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sometimes, <i>rom</i> and <i>romani</i> are spelled with a double <i>r</i>, i.e., <i>rrom</i> and <i>rromani</i>. In this case <i>rr</i> is used to represent the phoneme <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ʀ/</span> (also written as <i>ř</i> and <i>rh</i>), which in some Romani dialects has remained different from the one written with a single <i>r</i>. The <i>rr</i> spelling is common in certain institutions (such as the <a href="/wiki/Institut_national_des_langues_et_civilisations_orientales" title="Institut national des langues et civilisations orientales">INALCO Institute</a> in Paris), or used in certain countries, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, to distinguish from the <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">endonym</a>/<a href="/wiki/Homonym" title="Homonym">homonym</a> for <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a> (<i>sg. român, pl. români</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock2002xxi_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock2002xxi-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English_usage">English usage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: English usage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gypsy_wagon,_Grandborough_Fields_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1256879.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gypsy_wagon%2C_Grandborough_Fields_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1256879.jpg/260px-Gypsy_wagon%2C_Grandborough_Fields_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1256879.jpg" width="260" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gypsy_wagon%2C_Grandborough_Fields_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1256879.jpg/390px-Gypsy_wagon%2C_Grandborough_Fields_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1256879.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gypsy_wagon%2C_Grandborough_Fields_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1256879.jpg/520px-Gypsy_wagon%2C_Grandborough_Fields_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1256879.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="542" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gypsy_wagon,_Grandborough_Fields_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1256879.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Romani wagon pictured in 2009 in <a href="/wiki/Grandborough" title="Grandborough">Grandborough</a> (Grandborough Fields Road is a popular spot for travelling people)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the English language (according to the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a>), <i>Rom</i> is a noun (with the plural <i>Roma</i> or <i>Roms</i>) and an adjective, while <i>Romani</i> (<i>Romany</i>) is also a noun (with the plural <i>Romani</i>, <i>the Romani</i>, <i>Romanies</i> or <i>Romanis</i>) and an adjective. Both <i>Rom</i> and <i>Romani</i> have been in use in English since the 19th century as an alternative for Gypsy. <i>Romani</i> was initially spelled <i>Rommany</i>, then <i>Romany</i>, while today the <i>Romani</i> spelling is the most popular spelling. Occasionally, the double <i>r</i> spelling (e.g., <i>Rroma</i>, <i>Rromani</i>) mentioned above is also encountered in English texts.</p>
<p>The term <i>Roma</i> is increasingly encountered during recent decades,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> as a generic term for the Romani people.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Garner_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garner-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because all Romanies use the word <i>Romani</i> as an adjective, the term became a noun for the entire ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock2002xx_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock2002xx-74">[74]</a></sup> Today, the term <i>Romani</i> is used by some organizations&#160;–  including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the US Library of Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock2002xxi_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock2002xxi-68">[68]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> and other organizations consider that <i>Roma</i> is the correct term referring to all related groups, regardless of their country of origin, and recommend that <i>Romani</i> be restricted to the language and culture: <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_society_and_culture" title="Romani society and culture">Romani culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-words_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-words-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The standard assumption is that the <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">demonyms</a> of the Romani people, <a href="/wiki/Lom_people" title="Lom people">Lom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dom_people" title="Dom people">Dom</a> share the same origin.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_designations">Other designations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other designations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Gypsy_(term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsy (term)">Gypsy (term)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0525-0500-003,_Rheinland,_Sinti_und_Roma_mit_Wohnwagen_auf_Landstra%C3%9Fe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0525-0500-003%2C_Rheinland%2C_Sinti_und_Roma_mit_Wohnwagen_auf_Landstra%C3%9Fe.jpg/260px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0525-0500-003%2C_Rheinland%2C_Sinti_und_Roma_mit_Wohnwagen_auf_Landstra%C3%9Fe.jpg" width="260" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0525-0500-003%2C_Rheinland%2C_Sinti_und_Roma_mit_Wohnwagen_auf_Landstra%C3%9Fe.jpg/390px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0525-0500-003%2C_Rheinland%2C_Sinti_und_Roma_mit_Wohnwagen_auf_Landstra%C3%9Fe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0525-0500-003%2C_Rheinland%2C_Sinti_und_Roma_mit_Wohnwagen_auf_Landstra%C3%9Fe.jpg/520px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0525-0500-003%2C_Rheinland%2C_Sinti_und_Roma_mit_Wohnwagen_auf_Landstra%C3%9Fe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="623" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J0525-0500-003,_Rheinland,_Sinti_und_Roma_mit_Wohnwagen_auf_Landstra%C3%9Fe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Romani wagon in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a> in 1935</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The English term <i>Gypsy</i> (or <i>Gipsy</i>) originates from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a> <i>gypcian</i>, short for <i>Egipcien</i>. The Spanish term <i>Gitano</i> and French <i>Gitan</i> have similar etymologies. They are ultimately derived from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <span lang="grc">Αἰγύπτιοι</span> (<i>Aigyptioi</i>), meaning Egyptian, via <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>. This designation owes its existence to the belief, common in the Middle Ages, that the Romani, or some related group (such as the middle eastern <a href="/wiki/Dom_people" title="Dom people">Dom people</a>), were itinerant Egyptians.<sup id="cite_ref-Soulis_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soulis-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-White_1999_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White_1999-78">[78]</a></sup> According to one narrative they were exiled from Egypt as punishment for allegedly harbouring the <a href="/wiki/Child_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Child Jesus">infant Jesus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fraser1992_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fraser1992-79">[79]</a></sup> As described in <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugo" title="Victor Hugo">Victor Hugo</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunchback_of_Notre_Dame" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hunchback of Notre Dame">The Hunchback of Notre Dame</a></i>, the medieval French referred to the Romanies as <i>Egyptiens</i>. The word <i>Gypsy</i> in English has become so pervasive that many Romani organizations use it in their own organizational names.</p>
<p>This <a href="/wiki/Exonym_and_endonym" title="Exonym and endonym">exonym</a> is sometimes written with capital letter, to show that it designates an <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> However, the word is sometimes considered derogatory because of its negative and stereotypical associations.<sup id="cite_ref-Garner_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garner-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MerriamWebsterpocket1998_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MerriamWebsterpocket1998-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Baskin_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baskin-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RomaReport_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RomaReport-83">[83]</a></sup> The Council of Europe consider that 'Gypsy' or equivalent terms, as well as administrative terms such as 'Gens du Voyage' (referring in fact to an ethnic group but not acknowledging ethnic identification) are not in line with European recommendations.<sup id="cite_ref-words_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-words-66">[66]</a></sup> In North America, the word <i>Gypsy</i> is most commonly used as a reference to Romani ethnicity, though lifestyle and fashion are at times also referenced by using this word.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another common designation of the Romani people is <i>Cingane</i> (alt. Tsinganoi, Zigar, Zigeuner), which probably derives from <i><a href="/wiki/Athinganoi" title="Athinganoi">Athinganoi</a></i>, the name of a Christian sect with whom the Romani (or some related group) became associated in the Middle Ages.<sup id="cite_ref-White_1999_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White_1999-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Starr_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Starr-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_and_subgroups">Population and subgroups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Population and subgroups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romani_population">Romani population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Romani population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romani_populations" class="mw-redirect" title="Romani populations">Romani populations</a></div>
<p>For a variety of reasons, many Romanies choose not to register their ethnic identity in official censuses. There are an estimated four million Romani people in Europe (as of 2002),<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> although some high estimates by Romani organizations give numbers as high as 14 million.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Significant Romani populations are found in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, in some Central European states, in Spain, France, Russia and Ukraine. Several million more Romanies may live out of Europe, in particular in the Middle East and in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romani_subgroups">Romani subgroups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Romani subgroups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Like the Roma in general, many different <a href="/wiki/Ethnonym" title="Ethnonym">ethnonyms</a> are given to subgroups of Roma. Sometimes a subgroup uses more than one <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">endonym</a>, is commonly known by an <a href="/wiki/Exonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Exonym">exonym</a> and/or erroneously by the endonym of another subgroup. The only name approaching an all-encompassing self-description is <i>Rom</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup> Even when subgroups don't use the name, they all acknowledge a common origin and a dichotomy between themselves and <i><a href="/wiki/Gadjo_(non-Romani)" title="Gadjo (non-Romani)">Gadjo</a></i> (non-Roma).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup> For instance, while the main group of Roma in <a href="/wiki/List_of_territorial_entities_where_German_is_an_official_language" title="List of territorial entities where German is an official language">German-speaking countries</a> refer to themselves as <a href="/wiki/Sinti" title="Sinti">Sinti</a>, their name for their original language is <i>Romanes</i>.</p>
<p>Subgroups have been described as, in part, a result of the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_caste_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu caste system">Hindu caste system</a>, which the founding population of <i>Rom</i> almost certainly experienced in their South Asian <i><a href="/wiki/Urheimat" title="Urheimat">urheimat</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>

<p>Many groups use names apparently derived from the Romani word <i>kalo</i> or <i>calo</i>, meaning "black or "absorbing all light".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> This closely resembles words for "black" and/or "dark" in <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan</a> languages (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> काल <a href="/wiki/K%C4%81la_(time)#Etymology" title="Kāla (time)"><i>kāla</i></a>: "black", "of a dark colour").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup> Likewise the name of the <a href="/wiki/Domba" title="Domba">Dom</a> or Domba people of North India – to whom the Roma have genetic,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> cultural and linguistic links – has come to imply "dark-skinned", in some Indian languages.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Hence names such as <i>kale</i> and <i>calé</i> may have originated as an <a href="/wiki/Exonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Exonym">exonym</a> and/or euphemism for Roma.</p>
<p>Other endonyms for Romani include, for example:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ashkali_and_Balkan_Egyptians" title="Ashkali and Balkan Egyptians"><i>Ashkali</i></a> (or "Balkan Egyptians"  [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>]) – Albanian-speaking Roma communities in the Balkans<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bashald%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bashaldé (page does not exist)">Bashaldé</a></i> – <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Slovakia" title="Hungarians in Slovakia">Hungarian-Slovak</a> Roma diaspora in the US from the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Hancock2010_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hancock2010-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><b>Calé</b></i> is the <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">endonym</a> used by both the <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Spain" title="Romani people in Spain">Spanish Roma</a> (<i>gitanos</i>) and Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Portugal" title="Romani people in Portugal">Portuguese Roma</a> <i>ciganos</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-jurova_endonyma_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jurova_endonyma-98">[98]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Cal%C3%B3_language" title="Caló language">Caló</a></i> is "the language spoken by the <i>calé</i>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Greece" title="Romani people in Greece">Erlides</a></i> (also <i>Arlije</i>, <i>Yerlii</i> or <i>Arli</i>) in Greece</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Finnish_Kale" title="Finnish Kale"><i>Kaale</i></a>, in Finland and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jurova_endonyma_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jurova_endonyma-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kale_(Welsh_Romanies)" title="Kale (Welsh Romanies)">Kale</a>, <i>Kalá</i>, or <i>Valshanange</i> – <a href="/wiki/Welsh_English" title="Welsh English">Welsh English</a> endonym used by some Roma clans in Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Romanichal" title="Romanichal">Romanichal</a> also live in Wales.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Muslim_Roma" title="Muslim Roma"><i>Khorakhanè</i></a>, <i>Horahane</i> or <i>Xoraxai</i>, also known as "Turkish Roma" or "Muslim Roma" – <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Greece" title="Romani people in Greece">Greek Roma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Turkey" title="Romani people in Turkey">Turkish Roma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lalleri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lalleri (page does not exist)">Lalleri</a></i>, from <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, Germany, and the western <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> (including the former <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a>).</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Lovari" title="Lovari">Lovari</a></i>, from Hungary,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> known in Serbia as <i>Machvaya</i>, <i>Machavaya</i>, <i>Machwaya</i>, or <i>Macwaia</i>. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Luri" class="mw-redirect" title="Luri">Luri</a></i>, mainly in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Lyuli" title="Lyuli">Lyuli</a></i>, in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asian</a> countries.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Italy" title="Romani people in Italy">Rom</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Romania" title="Romani people in Romania"><i>Roma</i></a> in Romania, commonly known by majority <a href="/wiki/Romanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian people">ethnic Romanians</a> as <i>Țigani</i>, including many subgroups defined by occupation,&#160;:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boyash" title="Boyash">Boyash</a> also known as <i>Băieşi</i>, <i>Lingurari</i>, <i>Ludar</i>, <i>Ludari</i>, or <i>Rudari</i>, who coalesced in the <a href="/wiki/Apuseni_Mountains" title="Apuseni Mountains">Apuseni Mountains</a> of <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>. Boyash or <i>băieşi</i> is a Romanian word for "miners". <i>Lingurari</i> means "spoon makers",<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <i>Ludar</i>,<i>Ludari</i>, and<i>Rudari</i> may mean "woodworkers" or "miners".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> (There is a semantic overlap due to the <a href="/wiki/Homophony" title="Homophony">homophony</a> and/or merging of <a href="/wiki/Headword" title="Headword">lemmas</a> with different meanings from at least two different languages: the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> <i>rudar</i> miner, and <i>ruda</i> stick, staff, rod, bar, pole (in <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a> <i>rúd</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a> <i>rudă</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Churari&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Churari (page does not exist)">Churari</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> from Romanian <i>Ciurari</i>, "sieve makers", Zlătari "gold smiths"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ursari" title="Ursari">Ursari</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Animal_training#Wild_animals" title="Animal training">bear trainers</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">Moldovan</a>/<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a> <i>urs</i> "bear"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ungaritza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ungaritza (page does not exist)">Ungaritza</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Blacksmiths" class="mw-redirect" title="Blacksmiths">blacksmiths</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bladesmithh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bladesmithh (page does not exist)">bladesmithhs</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Argintari&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Argintari (page does not exist)">Argintari</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Silversmith" title="Silversmith">silversmiths</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aurari&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aurari (page does not exist)">Aurari</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Goldsmith" title="Goldsmith">goldsmiths</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florari&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Florari (page does not exist)">Florari</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Flower_seller" title="Flower seller">flower sellers</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/L%C4%83utari" title="Lăutari">Lăutari</a></i> singers.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Kalderash" title="Kalderash">Kalderash</a></i>, from Romanian<i>caldarar</i> meaning tinsmith, tinker, kettlemaker; also in <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Czech_Roma" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech Roma">Roma</a> or <i>Romové</i>, Czech Republic</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Slovak_Roma" class="mw-redirect" title="Slovak Roma">Roma</a> or <i>Romská</i>, Slovakia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romanichal" title="Romanichal">Romanichal</a>, in the United Kingdom,<sup id="cite_ref-jurova_endonyma_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jurova_endonyma-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup> emigrated also to the <a href="/wiki/Roma_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma in the United States">United States</a>, Canada and Australia<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_and_Swedish_Travellers" title="Norwegian and Swedish Travellers"><i>Romanisæl</i></a>, in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_France" title="Romani people in France"><i>Roms</i></a> or <i>Manouche</i> (from <i>manush</i> "people" in Romani) in France.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Romungro" class="mw-redirect" title="Romungro">Romungro</a></i> or Carpathian Romani from eastern Hungary and neighbouring parts of the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathians</a> <sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Sinti" title="Sinti">Sinti</a></i> or <i>Zinti</i>, predominantly in Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-jurova_endonyma_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jurova_endonyma-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Italy" title="Northern Italy">Northern Italy</a>; <i>Sinti</i> do not refer to themselves as Roma, although their language is called <i>Romanes</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003_91-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEH.C3.BCbshmanov.C3.A12003-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">Diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romani_diaspora" title="Romani diaspora">Romani diaspora</a></div>
<p>The Roma people have a number of distinct populations, the largest being the <a href="/wiki/Roma_(Romani_subgroup)" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma (Romani subgroup)">Roma</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cal%C3%A9_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Calé (disambiguation)">Iberian Calé or Caló</a>, who reached <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> about the early 12th century, from a migration out of northwestern <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> beginning about 600 years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-IsabelMendizabal_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IsabelMendizabal-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Comas_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comas-109">[109]</a></sup> They settled in present-day <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, by order of volume, and Spain. From the Balkans, they migrated throughout Europe and, in the nineteenth and later centuries, to the Americas. The Romani population in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> is estimated at more than one million.<sup id="cite_ref-time_note_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is no official or reliable count of the Romani populations worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Many Romani refuse to register their ethnic identity in official censuses for fear of discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Others are descendants of intermarriage with local populations and no longer identify only as Romani, or not at all.</p>
<p>As of the early 2000s, an estimated 3.8<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> to 9 million Romani people lived in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Asia Minor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> although some Romani organizations estimate numbers as high as 14 million.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Significant Romani populations are found in the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan peninsula">Balkan peninsula</a>, in some <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central European</a> states, in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>. The total number of Romani living outside Europe are primarily in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_and_North_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle East and North Africa">Middle East and North Africa</a> and in the Americas, and are estimated in total at more than two million. Some countries do not collect data by ethnicity.</p>
<p>The Romani people identify as distinct ethnicities based in part on territorial, cultural and <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialectal</a> differences, and self-designation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock20012_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock20012-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatras20025_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatras20025-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Names_of_the_Romani_People_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Names_of_the_Romani_People-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">Origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Origin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_the_Romani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Origin of the Romani people">Origin of the Romani people</a></div>
<p>Findings suggest an <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> origin for Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-IsabelMendizabal_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IsabelMendizabal-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Comas_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comas-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Because Romani groups did not keep chronicles of their history or have oral accounts of it, most hypotheses about the Romani's migration early history are based on linguistic theory.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> There is also no known record of a migration from India to Europe from medieval times that can be connected indisputably to Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatras200214_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatras200214-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shahnameh_legend"><i>Shahnameh</i> legend</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Shahnameh legend">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to a legend reported in <i><a href="/wiki/Shahnameh" title="Shahnameh">Shahnameh</a></i> and repeated by several modern authors, the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian" class="mw-redirect" title="Sasanian">Sasanian</a> king <a href="/wiki/Bahram_V" title="Bahram V">Bahrām V Gōr</a> learned towards the end of his reign (421–39) that the poor could not afford to enjoy music, and he asked the king of India to send him ten thousand <i>luris</i>, men and women, lute playing experts. When the luris arrived, Bahrām gave each one an ox and a donkey and a donkey-load of wheat so that they could live on agriculture and play music for free for the poor. But the luris ate the oxen and the wheat and came back a year later with their cheeks hollowed with hunger. The king, angered with their having wasted what he had given them, ordered them to pack up their bags and go wandering around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-GYPSY_i_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GYPSY_i-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Linguistic_evidence">Linguistic evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Linguistic evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The linguistic evidence has indisputably shown that roots of Romani language lie in India: the language has grammatical characteristics of Indian languages and shares with them a large part of the basic lexicon, for example, regarding body parts or daily routines.<sup id="cite_ref-mluvnice_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mluvnice-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>More exactly, Romani shares the basic lexicon with <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a>. It shares many phonetic features with <a href="/wiki/Marwari_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Marwari (language)">Marwari</a>, while its grammar is closest to <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hub1995_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hub1995-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Romani and <a href="/wiki/Domari_language" title="Domari language">Domari</a> share some similarities: <a href="/wiki/Agglutination" title="Agglutination">agglutination</a> of postpositions of the second Layer (or <a href="/wiki/Case_marking" class="mw-redirect" title="Case marking">case marking</a> clitics) to the nominal stem, concord markers for the past tense, the neutralisation of gender marking in the plural, and the use of the oblique case as an accusative.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatras200248_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatras200248-126">[126]</a></sup> This has prompted much discussion about the relationships between these two languages. Domari was once thought a "sister language" of Romani, the two languages having split after the departure from the Indian subcontinent&#160;–  but more recent research suggests that the differences between them are significant enough to treat them as two separate languages within the <a href="/wiki/Central_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Central zone">Central zone</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">Hindustani</a>) group of languages. The Dom and the Rom therefore likely descend from two different migration waves out of India, separated by several centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Domari_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Domari-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ROMANI_ORIGINS_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROMANI_ORIGINS-127">[127]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Numeral_(linguistics)" title="Numeral (linguistics)">Numerals</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domari_language" title="Domari language">Domari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lomavren" class="mw-redirect" title="Lomavren">Lomavren</a> languages, with <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> forms for comparison.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Note that Romani 7–9 are borrowed from Greek.</p>
