<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetic_evidence">Genetic evidence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Genetic evidence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Francisco_Iturrino_Two_Gypsies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Francisco_Iturrino_Two_Gypsies.jpg/200px-Francisco_Iturrino_Two_Gypsies.jpg" width="200" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Francisco_Iturrino_Two_Gypsies.jpg/300px-Francisco_Iturrino_Two_Gypsies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Francisco_Iturrino_Two_Gypsies.jpg/400px-Francisco_Iturrino_Two_Gypsies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2300" data-file-height="3273" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Francisco_Iturrino_Two_Gypsies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Two Gypsies in Spain, by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Iturrino" title="Francisco Iturrino">Francisco Iturrino</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Genetic findings in 2012 suggest the Romani originated in northwestern India and migrated as a group.<sup id="cite_ref-IsabelMendizabal_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IsabelMendizabal-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Comas_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comas-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> According to the study, the ancestors of present scheduled tribes and scheduled caste populations of <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">northern</a> <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, traditionally referred to collectively as the <a href="/wiki/%E1%B8%8Coma" class="mw-redirect" title="Ḍoma">Ḍoma</a>, are the likely ancestral populations of modern European Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> In December 2012, additional findings appeared to confirm the "Roma came from a single group that left northwestern India about 1,500 years ago."<sup id="cite_ref-Comas_109-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comas-109">[109]</a></sup> They reached the Balkans about 900 years ago<sup id="cite_ref-IsabelMendizabal_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IsabelMendizabal-108">[108]</a></sup> and then spread throughout Europe. The team found that, despite some isolation, the Roma were "genetically similar to other Europeans."<sup id="cite_ref-IsabelMendizabal_108-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IsabelMendizabal-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Comas_109-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comas-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Genetic research published in <i><a href="/wiki/European_Journal_of_Human_Genetics" title="European Journal of Human Genetics">European Journal of Human Genetics</a></i> "has revealed that over 70% of males belong to a single lineage that appears unique to the Roma."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>Genetic evidence supports the mediaeval migration from India. The Romani have been described as "a conglomerate of genetically isolated founder populations,"<sup id="cite_ref-Luba_Kalaydjieva_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luba_Kalaydjieva-132">[132]</a></sup> while a number of common <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mendelian_traits_in_humans" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Mendelian traits in humans">Mendelian</a> disorders among Romanies from all over Europe indicates "a common origin and <a href="/wiki/Founder_effect" title="Founder effect">founder effect</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Luba_Kalaydjieva_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luba_Kalaydjieva-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>A study from 2001 by Gresham et al. suggests "a limited number of related founders, compatible with a small group of migrants splitting from a distinct caste or tribal group."<sup id="cite_ref-David_Gresham_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-David_Gresham-134">[134]</a></sup> The same study found that "a single lineage… found across Romani populations, accounts for almost one-third of Romani males."<sup id="cite_ref-David_Gresham_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-David_Gresham-134">[134]</a></sup> A 2004 study by Morar et al. concluded that the Romani population "was founded approximately 32–40 generations ago, with secondary and tertiary founder events occurring approximately 16–25 generations ago."<sup id="cite_ref-Bharti_Morar_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bharti_Morar-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>Haplogroup H-M82 is a major lineage cluster in the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Romani" title="Balkan Romani">Balkan Romani</a> group, accounting for approximately 60% of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-Perecic2005_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perecic2005-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_H_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup H (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup H</a> is uncommon in Europe but present in the Indian subcontinent and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>.</p>
<p>A study of 444 people representing three different ethnic groups in the Republic of Macedonia found mtDNA haplogroups M5a1 and H7a1a were dominant in Romanies (13.7% and 10.3%, respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>Y-DNA composition of Romani in the Republic of Macedonia, based on 57 samples:<sup id="cite_ref-Pericic2005_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pericic2005-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_H_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup H (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup H</a> – 59.6%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_E_(Y-DNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup E (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup E</a> – 29.8%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_I_(Y-DNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup I (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup I</a> – 5.3%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup R (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup R</a> – 3.%, of which the half are <a href="/wiki/R1b" class="mw-redirect" title="R1b">R1b</a> and many are <a href="/wiki/R1a" class="mw-redirect" title="R1a">R1a</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_G_(Y-DNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup G (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup G</a> – 1.8%</li>
</ul>
<p>Y-DNA Haplogroup H1a occurs in Romani at frequencies 7-70%. Unlike ethnic Hungarians, among Hungarian and Slovakian Romani subpopulations, <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_E-V68" title="Haplogroup E-V68">Haplogroup E-M78</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_I1" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup I1">I1</a> usually occur above 10% and sometimes over 20%. While among Slovakian and <a href="/wiki/Tiszavasvari" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiszavasvari">Tiszavasvari</a> Romani the dominant haplogroup is H1a, among <a href="/wiki/Tokaj" title="Tokaj">Tokaj</a> Romani is <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_J2" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup J2">Haplogroup J2a</a> (23%), while among <a href="/wiki/Taktahark%C3%A1ny" title="Taktaharkány">Taktaharkány</a> Romani is <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_I-M438" title="Haplogroup I-M438">Haplogroup I2a</a> (21%).<sup id="cite_ref-s009.radikal.ru_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s009.radikal.ru-139">[139]</a></sup> Five, rather consistent founder lineages throughout the subpopulations, were found among Romani - J-M67 and J-M92 (J2), H-M52 (H1a1), and I-P259 (I1?). Haplogroup I-P259 as H is not found at frequencies of over 3 percent among host populations, while haplogroups E and I are absent in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. The lineages E-V13, I-P37 (I2a) and R-M17 (R1a) may represent gene flow from the host populations, excluding the Z93 branch of R1a, which is most frequent among Romani. Bulgarian, Romanian and Greek Romani are dominated by Haplogroup H-M82 (H1a1), while among Spanish Romani J2 is prevalent.<sup id="cite_ref-roman_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roman-140">[140]</a></sup> Among <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> Romani Haplogroup H prevails, while among <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> Romani, H drops to 7% and E-V13 rises to a prevailing level.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among non-Roma Europeans Haplogroup H is extremely rare, peaking at 5% among <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-s009.radikal.ru_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s009.radikal.ru-139">[139]</a></sup> although the carriers might be of Romani origin.<sup id="cite_ref-roman_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roman-140">[140]</a></sup> H is found at 2% among <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-researchgate.net_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchgate.net-142">[142]</a></sup> 2% among <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> 2% among Macedonians,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> 1% among <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> 1% among Bulgarians,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> 1% among Austrians and Swiss,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> 1% among <a href="/wiki/Turks" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Turks">Turks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-researchgate.net_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchgate.net-142">[142]</a></sup> According to autosomal analyses, between 2%<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> and 4% of ethnic Romanians belong to South Asian genetics, which is apart from Middle Eastern and East Asian,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> while Hungarians stood under 1%.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_migration_route">Possible migration route</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Possible migration route">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>They may have emerged from the modern Indian state of <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> migrating to the northwest (the <a href="/wiki/Punjab_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Punjab region">Punjab region</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sindh" title="Sindh">Sindh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baluchistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Baluchistan">Baluchistan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>) around 250 BC. Their subsequent westward migration, possibly in waves, is now believed to have occurred beginning in about AD 500.<sup id="cite_ref-Comas_109-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comas-109">[109]</a></sup> It has also been suggested that emigration from India may have taken place in the context of the raids by <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_of_Ghazni" title="Mahmud of Ghazni">Mahmud of Ghazni</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> As these soldiers were defeated, they were moved west with their families into the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>. The 11th century <i><a href="/wiki/Terminus_post_quem" title="Terminus post quem">terminus post quem</a></i> is due to the Romani language showing unambiguous features of the <a href="/wiki/Modern_Indo-Aryan" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Indo-Aryan">Modern Indo-Aryan</a> languages,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> precluding an emigration during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Indic" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Indic">Middle Indic</a> period.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Movimiento_gitano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Movimiento_gitano.jpg/330px-Movimiento_gitano.jpg" width="330" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Movimiento_gitano.jpg/495px-Movimiento_gitano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/Movimiento_gitano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="647" data-file-height="536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Movimiento_gitano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The migration of the Romanies through the Middle East and Northern Africa to Europe</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Romani_people" title="History of the Romani people">History of the Romani people</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_in_Europe">Arrival in Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Arrival in Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Though according to a 2012 genomic study, the Romani reached the Balkans as early as the 12th century,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> the first historical records of the Romani reaching south-eastern Europe are from the 14th century: in 1322, an Irish <a href="/wiki/Franciscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan">Franciscan</a> monk, <a href="/wiki/Symon_Semeonis" title="Symon Semeonis">Symon Semeonis</a> encountered a migrant group, "the descendants of <a href="/wiki/Cain" class="mw-redirect" title="Cain">Cain</a>", outside the town of <a href="/wiki/Heraklion" title="Heraklion">Heraklion</a> (Candia), in <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a>. Symon's account is probably the earliest surviving description by a Western chronicler of the Romani people in Europe. In 1350, <a href="/wiki/Ludolphus" class="mw-redirect" title="Ludolphus">Ludolphus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sudheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudheim">Sudheim</a> mentioned a similar people with a unique language whom he called <i>Mandapolos</i>, a word some think derives from the Greek word <i>mantes</i> (meaning prophet or fortune teller).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Around 1360, a <a href="/wiki/Fiefdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiefdom">fiefdom</a>, called the <i><a href="/wiki/Feudum_Acinganorum" title="Feudum Acinganorum">Feudum Acinganorum</a></i> was established in <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>, which mainly used Romani serfs and to which the Romani on the island were subservient.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> By the 1440s, they were recorded in Germany;<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> and by the 16th century, Scotland and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Some Romani migrated from <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persia</a> through North Africa, reaching the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in the 15th century. The two currents met in France.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spiezer_Schilling_749.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Spiezer_Schilling_749.jpg/220px-Spiezer_Schilling_749.jpg" width="220" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Spiezer_Schilling_749.jpg/330px-Spiezer_Schilling_749.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Spiezer_Schilling_749.jpg/440px-Spiezer_Schilling_749.jpg 2x" data-file-width="555" data-file-height="674" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spiezer_Schilling_749.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
First arrival of the Romanies outside <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">Bern</a> in the 15th century, described by the chronicler as <i>getoufte heiden</i> ("baptized heathens") and drawn with dark skin and wearing <a href="/wiki/Saracen" title="Saracen">Saracen</a>-style clothing and weapons (<a href="/wiki/Spiezer_Schilling" title="Spiezer Schilling">Spiezer Schilling</a>, p. 749)</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Modern_history">Early Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Early Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sclavi_Tiganesti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Sclavi_Tiganesti.jpg/170px-Sclavi_Tiganesti.jpg" width="170" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/Sclavi_Tiganesti.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="205" data-file-height="342" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sclavi_Tiganesti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An 1852 <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachian</a> poster advertising an auction of Romani slaves in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Their early history shows a mixed reception. Although 1385 marks the first recorded transaction for a Romani slave in <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a>, they were issued safe conduct by <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor Sigismund</a> in 1417.<sup id="cite_ref-kenrick_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenrick-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Romanies were ordered expelled from the <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Meissen" class="mw-redirect" title="Margraviate of Meissen">Meissen region</a> of Germany in 1416, <a href="/wiki/Lucerne" title="Lucerne">Lucerne</a> in 1471, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> in 1493, France in 1504, <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> in 1512, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> in 1525, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> in 1530 (see <a href="/wiki/Egyptians_Act_1530" title="Egyptians Act 1530">Egyptians Act 1530</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> in 1536.<sup id="cite_ref-kenrick_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenrick-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1510, any Romani found in Switzerland were ordered put to death, with similar rules established in England in 1554, and Denmark in 1589, whereas <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> began deportations of Romanies to its colonies in 1538.<sup id="cite_ref-kenrick_159-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenrick-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>A 1596 English statute, however, gave Romanies special privileges that other wanderers lacked; France passed a similar law in 1683. <a href="/wiki/Catherine_II_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Catherine II of Russia">Catherine the Great of Russia</a> declared the Romanies "crown slaves" (a status superior to <a href="/wiki/Serfs" class="mw-redirect" title="Serfs">serfs</a>), but also kept them out of certain parts of <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petersburg, Russia">the capital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Norman_Davies_1996_387.E2.80.93388_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norman_Davies_1996_387.E2.80.93388-160">[160]</a></sup> In 1595, <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Etefan_R%C4%83zvan" class="mw-redirect" title="Ştefan Răzvan">Ştefan Răzvan</a> overcame his birth into slavery, and became the <a href="/wiki/Voivode" title="Voivode">Voivode</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_Moldavian_rulers" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Moldavian rulers">Prince</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kenrick_159-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenrick-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Since a royal edict by <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Spain" title="Charles II of Spain">Charles II</a> in 1695, Spanish gypsies had been restricted to certain towns.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> An official edict in 1717 restricted them to only 75 towns and districts, so that they would not be concentrated in any one region. In the <a href="/wiki/Great_Gypsy_Round-up" title="Great Gypsy Round-up">Great Gypsy Round-up</a>, Romani were arrested and imprisoned in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Monarchy">Spanish Monarchy</a> in 1749.</p>
<p>Although some Romani could be kept as slaves in Wallachia and Moldavia until <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">abolition</a> in 1856, the majority traveled as free nomads with their wagons, as alluded to in the spoked wheel symbol in the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Romani_people" title="Flag of the Romani people">Romanies flag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock200125_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock200125-162">[162]</a></sup> Elsewhere in Europe, they were subject to <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a>, abduction of their children, and <a href="/wiki/Forced_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced labor">forced labor</a>. In England, Romani were sometimes expelled from small communities or hanged; in France, they were branded and their heads were shaved; in <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, the women were marked by their ears being severed. As a result, large groups of the Romani moved to the East, toward <a href="/wiki/Polish-Lithuanian_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth">Poland</a>, which was more tolerant, and Russia, where the Romani were treated more fairly as long as they paid the annual taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Romani began emigrating to North America in colonial times, with small groups recorded in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">French Louisiana</a>. Larger-scale <a href="/wiki/Roma_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma in the United States">Roma emigration to the United States</a> began in the 1860s, with groups of Romanichal from Great Britain. The largest number immigrated in the early 1900s, mainly from the Vlax group of <a href="/wiki/Kalderash" title="Kalderash">Kalderash</a>. Many Romani also settled in South America.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-52,_Asperg,_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-52%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg/260px-Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-52%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg" width="260" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-52%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg/390px-Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-52%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-52%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg/520px-Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-52%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="499" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-52,_Asperg,_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sinti" title="Sinti">Sinti</a> and other Romani about to be deported from Germany, May 22, 1940.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Porajmos</a></div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazis</a> embarked on a systematic <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> of the Romani, a process known in Romani as the <i><a href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Porajmos</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Milton_estimates_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milton_estimates-164">[164]</a></sup> Romanies were marked for extermination and sentenced to forced labor and imprisonment in <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camps</a>.</p>
<p>They were often killed on sight, especially by the <a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a> (paramilitary death squads) on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> The total number of victims has been variously estimated at between 220,000 and 1,500,000; even the lower figure would make the Porajmos one of the largest mass killings in history.<sup id="cite_ref-hancock2005_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hancock2005-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>The treatment of Romani in Nazi partner states differed markedly. In the (Independent State of Croatia|<a href="/wiki/NDH" class="mw-redirect" title="NDH">NDH</a>) the separatist <a href="/wiki/Ustasa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ustasa">Ustasa</a> organization physically annihilated around 25,000 people, almost the entire Roma population. The concentration camp system of <a href="/wiki/Jasenovac_concentration_camp" title="Jasenovac concentration camp">Jasenovac</a>, run by the Ustasa militia and the Croat political police, were responsible for the deaths of between 15,000 and 20,000 Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-1945">Post-1945</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Post-1945">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, they were labeled a "socially degraded stratum," and Romani women were sterilized as part of a state policy to reduce their population. This policy was implemented with large financial incentives, threats of denying future welfare payments, with misinformation, or after administering drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESilverman1995_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESilverman1995-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelsinki_Watch1991_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelsinki_Watch1991-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>An official inquiry from the Czech Republic, resulting in a report (December 2005), concluded that the Communist authorities had practiced an assimilation policy towards Romanis, which "included efforts by social services to control the birth rate in the Romani community." "The problem of sexual sterilisation carried out in the Czech Republic, either with improper motivation or illegally, exists," said the Czech Public Defender of Rights, recommending state compensation for women affected between 1973 and 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> New cases were revealed up until 2004, in both the Czech Republic and Slovakia. Germany, Norway, Sweden and Switzerland "all have histories of coercive sterilization of minorities and other groups."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_traditional_culture">Society and traditional culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Society and traditional culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romani_society_and_culture" title="Romani society and culture">Romani society and culture</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
