</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Gipsy_Family_Fac_simile_of_a_Woodcut_in_the_Cosmographie_Universelle_of_Munster_in_folio_Basle_1552.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/A_Gipsy_Family_Fac_simile_of_a_Woodcut_in_the_Cosmographie_Universelle_of_Munster_in_folio_Basle_1552.png/220px-A_Gipsy_Family_Fac_simile_of_a_Woodcut_in_the_Cosmographie_Universelle_of_Munster_in_folio_Basle_1552.png" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/A_Gipsy_Family_Fac_simile_of_a_Woodcut_in_the_Cosmographie_Universelle_of_Munster_in_folio_Basle_1552.png/330px-A_Gipsy_Family_Fac_simile_of_a_Woodcut_in_the_Cosmographie_Universelle_of_Munster_in_folio_Basle_1552.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/A_Gipsy_Family_Fac_simile_of_a_Woodcut_in_the_Cosmographie_Universelle_of_Munster_in_folio_Basle_1552.png/440px-A_Gipsy_Family_Fac_simile_of_a_Woodcut_in_the_Cosmographie_Universelle_of_Munster_in_folio_Basle_1552.png 2x" data-file-width="1338" data-file-height="833" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Gipsy_Family_Fac_simile_of_a_Woodcut_in_the_Cosmographie_Universelle_of_Munster_in_folio_Basle_1552.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sebastian_M%C3%BCnster" title="Sebastian Münster">Münster, Sebastian</a> (1552), "A Gipsy Family", The <a href="/wiki/Cosmographia_(Sebastian_M%C3%BCnster)" title="Cosmographia (Sebastian Münster)"><i>Cosmographia</i></a> (facsimile of a woodcut), Basle.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The traditional Romanies place a high value on the <a href="/wiki/Extended_family" title="Extended family">extended family</a>. <a href="/wiki/Virginity" title="Virginity">Virginity</a> is essential in unmarried women. Both men and women often marry young; there has been controversy in several countries over the Romani practice of <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">child marriage</a>. Romani law establishes that the man's family must pay a <a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">bride price</a> to the bride's parents, but only traditional families still follow this rule.</p>
<p>Once married, the woman joins the husband's family, where her main job is to tend to her husband's and her children's needs, as well as to take care of her in-laws. The power structure in the traditional Romani household has at its top the oldest man or grandfather, and men in general have more authority than women. Women gain respect and authority as they get older. Young wives begin gaining authority once they have children.</p>
<p>Romani <a href="/wiki/Social_behavior" title="Social behavior">social behavior</a> is strictly regulated by Hindu purity laws<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> ("marime" or "marhime"), still respected by most Roma (and by most older generations of <a href="/wiki/Sinti" title="Sinti">Sinti</a>). This regulation affects many aspects of life, and is applied to actions, people and things: parts of <a href="/wiki/Human_anatomy" class="mw-redirect" title="Human anatomy">the human body</a> are considered impure: the <a href="/wiki/Sex_organ" title="Sex organ">genital organs</a> (because they produce emissions), as well as the rest of the lower body. Clothes for the lower body, as well as the clothes of <a href="/wiki/Menstruation" title="Menstruation">menstruating</a> women, are washed separately. Items used for eating are also washed in a different place. Childbirth is considered impure, and must occur outside the dwelling place. The mother is considered impure for forty days after giving birth.</p>
<p>Death is considered impure, and affects the whole family of the dead, who remain impure for a period of time. In contrast to the practice of <a href="/wiki/Cremation" title="Cremation">cremating</a> the dead, Romani dead must be buried.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Cremation and burial are both known from the time of the <a href="/wiki/Rigveda" title="Rigveda">Rigveda</a>, and both are widely practiced in <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> today (although the tendency is for Hindus to practice cremation, while some communities in South India tend to bury their dead).<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Some animals are also considered impure, for instance cats because they lick their hindquarters. Horses, in contrast, are not considered impure because they cannot do so.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock200181_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock200181-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belonging_and_exclusion">Belonging and exclusion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Belonging and exclusion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Romanipen" title="Romanipen">Romanipen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gadjo_(non-Romani)" title="Gadjo (non-Romani)">Gadjo (non-Romani)</a></div>
<p><b>Romanipen</b> (also <i>romanypen</i>, <i>romanipe</i>, <i>romanype</i>, <i>romanimos</i>, <i>romaimos</i>, <i>romaniya</i>) is a complicated term of Romani philosophy that means totality of the Romani spirit, <a href="/wiki/Romani_society_and_culture" title="Romani society and culture">Romani culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kris_(Romani_court)" title="Kris (Romani court)">Romani Law</a>, being a Romani, a set of Romani strains.</p>
<p>An ethnic Romani is considered a <a href="/wiki/Gadjo_(non-Romani)" title="Gadjo (non-Romani)">Gadjo (non-Romani)</a> in the Romani society if he has no Romanipen. Sometimes a non-Romani may be considered a Romani if he has Romanipen. Usually this is an adopted child. As a concept, Romanipen has been the subject of interest to numerous academic observers. It has been hypothesized that it owes more to a <a href="/wiki/Cultural_framework" title="Cultural framework">framework of culture</a> rather than simply an adherence to historically received rules.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tziganes_aux_Saintes-Maries_de_la_Mer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Tziganes_aux_Saintes-Maries_de_la_Mer.jpg/290px-Tziganes_aux_Saintes-Maries_de_la_Mer.jpg" width="290" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Tziganes_aux_Saintes-Maries_de_la_Mer.jpg/435px-Tziganes_aux_Saintes-Maries_de_la_Mer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Tziganes_aux_Saintes-Maries_de_la_Mer.jpg/580px-Tziganes_aux_Saintes-Maries_de_la_Mer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2441" data-file-height="1654" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tziganes_aux_Saintes-Maries_de_la_Mer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Christian Romanies during the pilgrimage at <a href="/wiki/Saintes-Maries-de-la-Mer" title="Saintes-Maries-de-la-Mer">Saintes-Maries-de-la-Mer</a> in France, 1980s</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some Romani people are Christian, others Muslim, some others have their own religion and political organization.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beliefs">Beliefs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Beliefs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The ancestors of modern-day Romani people were previously <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>, but adopted Christianity or Islam depending on their respective regions they had migrated through.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Roma" title="Muslim Roma">Muslim Roma</a> are found in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, forming a very significant proportion of the Romani people. In neighboring countries such as <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> most of the Romani inhabitants follow the practice of <a href="/wiki/Orthodoxy" title="Orthodoxy">Orthodoxy</a>. It is likely that the adherence to differing religions prevented families from engaging in intermarriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Boretzky_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boretzky-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Deities_and_saints">Deities and saints</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Deities and saints">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ceferino_Gim%C3%A9nez_Malla" title="Ceferino Giménez Malla">Blessed Ceferino Giménez Malla</a> is considered a patron saint of the Romani people in Roman Catholicism.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saint_Sarah" title="Saint Sarah">Saint Sarah</a>, or Kali Sara, has also been venerated as a patron saint in the same manner as the Blessed Ceferino Giménez Malla. Since the turn of the 21st century, <a href="/wiki/Kali" title="Kali">Kali</a> Sara is understood to have been an Indian deity brought from India by the refugee ancestors of the Roma people; as the Roma became Christianized, she was absorbed in a syncretic way and worshipped as a saint.<sup id="cite_ref-lee_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lee-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mother Goddess figurines have been found in the excavations of the <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation" title="Indus Valley Civilisation">Indus Valley Civilisation</a> in Mohenjo Daro and Harappa, in the Sindh – Punjab – Haryana area [Some Romani claim Punjab is their original habitat], and Kali Mata [Mother Kali] is still worshipped in India, particularly by the Hindus. Therefore, Saint Sarah is now increasingly being considered as "a Romani Goddess, the Protectress of the Roma" and an "indisputable link with Mother India".<sup id="cite_ref-lee_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lee-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-radoc.net_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radoc.net-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceremonies_and_practices">Ceremonies and practices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Ceremonies and practices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Romanies often adopt the dominant religion of their host country in the event that a ceremony associated with a formal religious institution is necessary, such as a baptism or funeral (their particular belief systems and indigenous religion and worship remain preserved regardless of such adoption processes). The Roma continue to practice "<a href="/wiki/Shaktism" title="Shaktism">Shaktism</a>", a practice with origins in India, whereby a female consort is required for the worship of a god. Adherence to this practice means that for the Roma who worship the Christian God, prayer is conducted through the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a>, or her mother, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anne" title="Saint Anne">Saint Anne</a>&#160;–  Shaktism continues over one thousand years after the people's separation from India.<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>Besides the Roma elders, who serve as spiritual leaders, priests, churches, or bibles do not exist among the Romanies&#160;–  the only exception is the Pentecostal Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Balkans">Balkans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Balkans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_Studio_Shot_of_European_in_Gypsy_Costume_One_of_274_Vintage_Photographs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Studio_Shot_of_European_in_Gypsy_Costume_One_of_274_Vintage_Photographs.jpg/220px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Studio_Shot_of_European_in_Gypsy_Costume_One_of_274_Vintage_Photographs.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Studio_Shot_of_European_in_Gypsy_Costume_One_of_274_Vintage_Photographs.jpg/330px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Studio_Shot_of_European_in_Gypsy_Costume_One_of_274_Vintage_Photographs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Studio_Shot_of_European_in_Gypsy_Costume_One_of_274_Vintage_Photographs.jpg/440px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Studio_Shot_of_European_in_Gypsy_Costume_One_of_274_Vintage_Photographs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="703" data-file-height="556" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_Studio_Shot_of_European_in_Gypsy_Costume_One_of_274_Vintage_Photographs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Costume of a Romani woman (most likely <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Roma" title="Muslim Roma">Muslim Roma</a>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the Roma communities that have resided in the Balkans for numerous centuries, often referred to as "Turkish Gypsies", the following histories apply for religious beliefs:</p>
<ul>
<li>Albania – The majority of Albania's Roma people are Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></li>
<li>Bosnia and Herzegovina and Montenegro – Islam is the dominant religion amongst the Roma.<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></li>
<li>Bulgaria – In northwestern Bulgaria, in addition to Sofia and Kyustendil, Christianity is the dominant faith among Romani people, though a major conversion to Eastern Orthodox Christianity among Romani people has occurred. In southeastern Bulgaria, Islam is the dominant religion among Romani people, with a smaller section of the Romani population, declaring themselves as "Turks", continuing to mix ethnicity with Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></li>
<li>Croatia – Following the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, a large number of Muslim Roma relocated to Croatia (the majority moving from Kosovo).<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></li>
<li>Greece – The descendants of groups, such as Sepečides or Sevljara, Kalpazaja, Filipidži and others, living in Athens, Thessaloniki, central Greece and Aegean Macedonia are mostly Orthodox Christians, with Islamic beliefs held by a minority of the population. Following the Peace Treaty of Lausanne of 1923, many Muslim Roma moved to Turkey in the subsequent population exchange between Turkey and Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Muslim_Gypsies_from_Bosnia,_illustration,_1901.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Muslim_Gypsies_from_Bosnia%2C_illustration%2C_1901.jpg/180px-Muslim_Gypsies_from_Bosnia%2C_illustration%2C_1901.jpg" width="180" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Muslim_Gypsies_from_Bosnia%2C_illustration%2C_1901.jpg/270px-Muslim_Gypsies_from_Bosnia%2C_illustration%2C_1901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Muslim_Gypsies_from_Bosnia%2C_illustration%2C_1901.jpg/360px-Muslim_Gypsies_from_Bosnia%2C_illustration%2C_1901.jpg 2x" data-file-width="461" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Muslim_Gypsies_from_Bosnia,_illustration,_1901.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Muslim Romanies in <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> (around 1900)</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Kosovo – The vast majority of the Roma population in Kosovo is Muslim.<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></li>
<li>Macedonia – The majority of Roma people are followers of <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Islam in Macedonia">Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></li>
<li>Romania – According to the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Romania" title="Demographic history of Romania">2002 census</a>, the majority of Romani minority living in Romania are <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Orthodox_Church" title="Romanian Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a>, while 6.4% are <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal_Union_of_Romania" title="Pentecostal Union of Romania">Pentecostals</a>, 3.8% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Romania" title="Roman Catholicism in Romania">Roman Catholics</a>, 3% <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Church_in_Romania" title="Reformed Church in Romania">Reformed</a>, 1.1% <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Church_United_with_Rome,_Greek-Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian Church United with Rome, Greek-Catholic">Greek Catholics</a>, 0.9% <a href="/wiki/Baptist_Union_of_Romania" title="Baptist Union of Romania">Baptists</a>, 0.8% <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Union_Conference_of_Seventh-day_Adventists" title="Romanian Union Conference of Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-Day Adventists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Dobruja" title="Dobruja">Dobruja</a>, there is a small community that are <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Romania" title="Islam in Romania">Muslim</a> and also speak Turkish.<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></li>
<li>Serbia – Most Roma people in Serbia are Orthodox Christian, but there are some Muslim Roma in Southern Serbia, who are mainly refugees from Kosovo.<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_regions">Other regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Other regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and Russia the Roma populations are also Muslim as the families of Balkan migrants continue to live in these locations. Their ancestors settled on the Crimean peninsula during the 17th and 18th centuries, but then migrated to Ukraine, southern Russia and the Povolzhie (along the Volga River). Formally, Islam is the religion that these communities align themselves with and the people are recognized for their <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/staunch" class="extiw" title="wikt:staunch">staunch</a> preservation of the Romani language and identity.<sup id="cite_ref-Roma_185-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roma-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most Eastern European Romanies are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Those in Western Europe and the <a href="/wiki/Roma_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma in the United States">United States</a> are mostly Roman Catholic or <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>&#160;–  in southern Spain, many Romanies are <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal</a>, but this is a small minority that has emerged in contemporary times.<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_183-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-183">[183]</a></sup> In Egypt, the Romanies are split into Christian and Muslim populations.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romani_music" title="Romani music">Romani music</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Romungro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Romungro.jpg/180px-Romungro.jpg" width="180" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Romungro.jpg/270px-Romungro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/Romungro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="315" data-file-height="504" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Romungro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Young Hungarian Romani performing a traditional dance</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Romani music plays an important role in Central and Eastern European countries such as Croatia, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Serbia, Montenegro, Bulgaria, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>, Albania, Hungary, Slovakia, Slovenia and Romania, and the style and performance practices of Romani musicians have influenced European <a href="/wiki/List_of_classical_music_composers" class="mw-redirect" title="List of classical music composers">classical composers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Franz_Liszt" title="Franz Liszt">Franz Liszt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/L%C4%83utari" title="Lăutari">lăutari</a></i> who perform at traditional Romanian weddings are virtually all Romani.</p>
<p>Probably the most internationally prominent contemporary performers in the <i>lăutari</i> tradition are <a href="/wiki/Taraful_Haiducilor" class="mw-redirect" title="Taraful Haiducilor">Taraful Haiducilor</a>. Bulgaria's popular "wedding music", too, is almost exclusively performed by Romani musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Papasov" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivo Papasov">Ivo Papasov</a>, a virtuoso clarinetist closely associated with this genre and Bulgarian pop-folk singer <a href="/wiki/Azis" title="Azis">Azis</a>.</p>
<p>Many famous classical musicians, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian people">Hungarian</a> pianist <a href="/wiki/Georges_Cziffra" class="mw-redirect" title="Georges Cziffra">Georges Cziffra</a>, are Romani, as are many prominent performers of <a href="/wiki/Manele" title="Manele">manele</a>. <a href="/wiki/Zdob_%C5%9Fi_Zdub" class="mw-redirect" title="Zdob şi Zdub">Zdob şi Zdub</a>, one of the most prominent rock bands in <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, although not Romanies themselves, draw heavily on Romani music, as do <a href="/wiki/Spitalul_de_Urgen%C5%A3%C4%83" class="mw-redirect" title="Spitalul de Urgenţă">Spitalul de Urgenţă</a> in Romania, <a href="/wiki/Shantel" title="Shantel">Shantel</a> in Germany, <a href="/wiki/Goran_Bregovi%C4%87" title="Goran Bregović">Goran Bregović</a> in Serbia, <a href="/wiki/Darko_Rundek" title="Darko Rundek">Darko Rundek</a> in Croatia, <a href="/wiki/Beirut_(band)" title="Beirut (band)">Beirut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gogol_Bordello" title="Gogol Bordello">Gogol Bordello</a> in the United States.</p>
<p>Another tradition of Romani music is the genre of the Romani <a href="/wiki/Brass_band" title="Brass band">brass band</a>, with such notable practitioners as <a href="/wiki/Boban_Markovi%C4%87" title="Boban Marković">Boban Marković</a> of Serbia, and the brass <i>lăutari</i> groups <a href="/wiki/Fanfare_Cioc%C4%83rlia" title="Fanfare Ciocărlia">Fanfare Ciocărlia</a> and Fanfare din Cozmesti of Romania.</p>
<p>Many musical instruments like violins and guitars are said<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (February 2015)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to have originated from the Romani. Many dances such as the flamenco of Spain and Oriental dances of Egypt are also said to have originated from them.<sup id="cite_ref-Gypsy_dance_origin_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gypsy_dance_origin-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>The distinctive sound of Romani music has also strongly influenced <a href="/wiki/Bolero" title="Bolero">bolero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">flamenco</a> (especially <i><a href="/wiki/Cante_jondo" title="Cante jondo">cante jondo</a></i>) in Europe. European-style <a href="/wiki/Gypsy_jazz" title="Gypsy jazz">gypsy jazz</a> ("jazz Manouche" or "Sinti jazz") is still widely practiced among the original creators (the Romanie People); one who acknowledged this artistic debt was guitarist <a href="/wiki/Django_Reinhardt" title="Django Reinhardt">Django Reinhardt</a>. Contemporary artists in this tradition known internationally include <a href="/wiki/Stochelo_Rosenberg" title="Stochelo Rosenberg">Stochelo Rosenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bir%C3%A9li_Lagr%C3%A8ne" title="Biréli Lagrène">Biréli Lagrène</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Rosenberg" title="Jimmy Rosenberg">Jimmy Rosenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paulus_Sch%C3%A4fer" title="Paulus Schäfer">Paulus Schäfer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tchavolo_Schmitt" title="Tchavolo Schmitt">Tchavolo Schmitt</a>.</p>
<p>The Romanies of Turkey have achieved musical acclaim from national and local audiences. Local performers usually perform for special holidays. Their music is usually performed on instruments such as the <a href="/wiki/Goblet_drum" title="Goblet drum">darbuka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clarinet" title="Clarinet">gırnata</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%BCmb%C3%BC%C5%9F" title="Cümbüş">cümbüş</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-family_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-family-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_art_and_culture">Contemporary art and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Contemporary art and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romani_contemporary_art" title="Romani contemporary art">Romani contemporary art</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Romani_contemporary_art" title="Romani contemporary art">Romani contemporary art</a> is art created by Romani people. It emerged at the climax of the process that began in <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a> in the late-1980s, when the interpretation of the cultural practice of minorities was enabled by a paradigm shift, commonly referred to in specialist literature as the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_turn" title="Cultural turn">Cultural turn</a>. The idea of the "cultural turn" was introduced; and this was also the time when the notion of cultural democracy became crystallized in the debates carried on at various public forums. <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">Civil society</a> gained strength, and civil politics appeared, which is a prerequisite for cultural democracy. This shift of attitude in scholarly circles derived from concerns specific not only to ethnicity, but also to society, gender and class.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a></div>
<p>Most Romani speak one of several dialects of the <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan</a> language, with roots in Sanskrit. They also often speak the languages of the countries they live in. Typically, they also incorporate <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calque" title="Calque">calques</a> into Romani from the languages of those countries and especially words for terms that the Romani language does not have. Most of the <i>Ciganos</i> of Portugal, the <a href="/wiki/Gitanos" class="mw-redirect" title="Gitanos">Gitanos</a> of Spain, the <a href="/wiki/Romanichal" title="Romanichal">Romanichal</a> of the UK, and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_and_Swedish_Travellers" title="Norwegian and Swedish Travellers">Scandinavian Travellers</a> have lost their <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a> of pure Romani, and respectively speak the <a href="/wiki/Mixed_language" title="Mixed language">mixed languages</a> <a href="/wiki/Cal%C3%B3_(Spanish_Romani)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caló (Spanish Romani)">Caló</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Angloromany" class="mw-redirect" title="Angloromany">Angloromany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scandoromani" class="mw-redirect" title="Scandoromani">Scandoromani</a>. Most of the speaker communities in these regions consist of later immigrants from eastern or central Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Manchester_Rom_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manchester_Rom-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are no concrete statistics for the number of <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a> speakers, both in Europe and globally. However, a conservative estimation has been made at 3.5 million speakers in Europe and a further 500,000 elsewhere,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> although the actual number may be considerably higher. This makes Romani the second largest <a href="/wiki/Minority_language" title="Minority language">minority language</a> in Europe, behind <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Manchester_Rom_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manchester_Rom-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>In relation to dialect diversity, Romani works in the same way as most other European languages.<sup id="cite_ref-The_status_of_Romani_in_Europe_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_status_of_Romani_in_Europe-196">[196]</a></sup> Cross-dialect communication is dominated by the following features:</p>
<ul>
<li>All <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a> speakers are <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">bilingual</a>, and are accustomed to borrowing words or phrases from a <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">second language</a>; this makes it difficult when trying to communicate with Romanis from different countries</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a> was traditionally a <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a> shared between extended family and a close-knit community. This has resulted in the inability to comprehend <a href="/wiki/Dialects" class="mw-redirect" title="Dialects">dialects</a> from other countries. This is the reason Romani is sometimes associated as being number of different languages.</li>
<li>There is no tradition or example of a literary standard for Romani speakers to use as a guideline for their language use.<sup id="cite_ref-The_status_of_Romani_in_Europe_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_status_of_Romani_in_Europe-196">[196]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Persecutions">Persecutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Persecutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Antiziganism" title="Antiziganism">Antiziganism</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_persecution">Historical persecution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Historical persecution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the most enduring persecutions against the Romani people was their being enslaved. <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_medieval_Europe" title="Slavery in medieval Europe">Slavery was widely practiced in medieval Europe</a>, including the territory of present-day Romania from before the founding of the principalities of <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> in the 13–14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Achim_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Achim-197">[197]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Legislation decreed that all the Romani living in these states, as well as any others who immigrated there, were classified as slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Slavery was gradually <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">abolished</a> during the 1840s and 1850s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAchim2004_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAchim2004-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The exact origins of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Romania" title="Slavery in Romania">slavery</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Danubian_Principalities" title="Danubian Principalities">Danubian Principalities</a> are not known. There is some debate over whether the Romani people came to Wallachia and Moldavia as free men or were brought as slaves. Historian <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Iorga" title="Nicolae Iorga">Nicolae Iorga</a> associated the Roma people's arrival with the 1241 <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">Mongol invasion of Europe</a> and considered their slavery as a vestige of that era, in which the <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a> took the Roma as slaves from the <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a> and preserved their status to use their labor. Other historians believe that the Romani were enslaved, while captured during the battles, with the Tatars. The practice of enslaving war prisoners may also have been adopted from the Mongols.<sup id="cite_ref-Achim_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Achim-197">[197]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Some Romani may have been slaves or auxiliary troops of the Mongols or Tatars, but most of them migrated from south of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> at the end of the 14th century, some time after the <a href="/wiki/Foundation_of_Wallachia" title="Foundation of Wallachia">foundation of Wallachia</a>. By then, the institution of slavery was already established in Moldavia and possibly in both principalities. After the Roma migrated into the area, slavery became a widespread practice by the majority population. The <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatar</a> slaves, smaller in numbers, were eventually merged into the Roma population.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some branches of the Romani people reached Western Europe in the 15th century, fleeing as refugees from the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> conquest of the Balkans.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Although the Romani were refugees from the conflicts in southeastern Europe, they were often suspected by certain populations in the West of being associated with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">Ottoman invasion</a> because of their physical features seemed related to the Turks. (The <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(Holy_Roman_Empire)#The_Reichstag_in_the_Holy_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Reichstag (Holy Roman Empire)">Imperial Diet</a> at Landau and Freiburg in 1496–1498 declared that the Romani were spies of the Turks). In Western Europe, such suspicions and discrimination against a people who were a visible minority resulted in persecution, often violent, with efforts to achieve <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> until the modern era. In times of social tension, the Romani suffered as scapegoats; for instance, they were accused of bringing the plague during times of <a href="/wiki/Epidemics" class="mw-redirect" title="Epidemics">epidemics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1749, Spain conducted <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Roundup_of_Gypsies_(1749)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Great Roundup of Gypsies (1749)"><i>The Great Roundup</i></a> of <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Spain" title="Romani people in Spain">Romani</a> (Gitanos) in its territory. The Spanish Crown ordered a nationwide raid that led to the break-up of families as all able-bodied men were interned into forced labor camps in a half-hearted attempt at ethnic cleansing. The measure was eventually reversed and the Gypsies were freed as protests began to arise in different communities, sedentary gypsies being highly esteemed and protected in rural Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later in the 19th century, Romani immigration was forbidden on a racial basis in areas outside Europe, mostly in the English-speaking world. (Argentina in 1880 prohibited immigration by Roma, as did the United States in 1885.)<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-48,_Asperg,_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-48%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg/260px-Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-48%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg" width="260" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-48%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg/390px-Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-48%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-48%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg/520px-Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-48%2C_Asperg%2C_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="539" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_R_165_Bild-244-48,_Asperg,_Deportation_von_Sinti_und_Roma.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Deportation of Roma from <a href="/wiki/Asperg" title="Asperg">Asperg</a>, Germany, 1940 (photograph by the <i>Rassenhygienische Forschungsstelle</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forced_assimilation">Forced assimilation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Forced assimilation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a> under <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Theresa of Austria">Maria Theresa</a> (1740–1780), a series of decrees tried to force the Romanies to <a href="/wiki/Sedentism" title="Sedentism">permanently settle</a>, removed rights to horse and wagon ownership (1754), renamed them as "New Citizens" and forced Romani boys into military service if they had no trade (1761), forced them to register with the local authorities (1767), and prohibited marriage between Romanies (1773). Her successor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Josef II</a> prohibited the wearing of traditional Romani clothing and the use of the Romani language, punishable by flogging.<sup id="cite_ref-samer_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samer-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Spain, attempts to assimilate the Gitanos were under way as early as 1619, when Gitanos were forcibly settled, the use of the Romani language was prohibited, Gitano men and women were sent to separate workhouses and their children sent to orphanages. <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">King Charles III</a> took on a more progressive attitude to Gitano assimilation, proclaiming their equal rights as Spanish citizens and ending official denigration based on their race. While he prohibited the nomadic lifestyle, the use of the <a href="/wiki/Cal%C3%B3_(Spanish_Romani)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caló (Spanish Romani)">Calo language</a>, Romani clothing, their trade in horses and other itinerant trades, he also forbade any form of discrimination against them or barring them from the guilds. The use of the word <i>gitano</i> was also forbidden to further assimilation, substituted for "New Castilian", which was also applied to former Jews and Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most historians agree that Charles III pragmática failed due to three main reasons, ultimately derived from its implementation outside major cities and in marginal areas: The difficulty the Gitano community faced in changing its nomadic lifestyle, the marginal lifestyle in which the community had been driven by society and the serious difficulties of applying the pragmática in the fields of education and work. One author ascribes its failure to the overall rejection by the wider population of the integration of the Gitanos.<sup id="cite_ref-samer_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samer-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other examples of forced assimilation include <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, where a law was passed in 1896 permitting the state to remove children from their parents and place them in state institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> This resulted in some 1,500 Romani children being taken from their parents in the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holocaust">Holocaust</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Holocaust">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Porajmos</a></div>
<p>The persecution of the Romanies reached a peak during World War II in the <i>Porajmos</i>, the genocide perpetrated by the <a href="/wiki/Nazis" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazis">Nazis</a> during <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>. In 1935, the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_laws" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg laws">Nuremberg laws</a> stripped the Romani people living in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> of their citizenship, after which they were subjected to violence, imprisonment in <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camps</a> and later genocide in <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a>. The policy was extended in areas occupied by the Nazis during the war, and it was also applied by their allies, notably the Independent State of Croatia, Romania and Hungary.</p>
<p>Because no accurate pre-war census figures exist for the Romanis, it is impossible to accurately assess the actual number of victims. <a href="/wiki/Ian_Hancock" title="Ian Hancock">Ian Hancock</a>, director of the Program of Romani Studies at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">University of Texas at Austin</a>, proposes a figure of up to a million and a half, while an estimate of between 220,000 and 500,000 was made by Sybil Milton, formerly senior historian of the U.S. Holocaust Memorial Museum.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[a]</a></sup> In Central Europe, the extermination in the <a href="/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia">Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia</a> was so thorough that the <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Romani" title="Bohemian Romani">Bohemian Romani</a> language became extinct.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_issues">Contemporary issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Contemporary issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Romani_population_average_estimate.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Romani_population_average_estimate.png/260px-Romani_population_average_estimate.png" width="260" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Romani_population_average_estimate.png/390px-Romani_population_average_estimate.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Romani_population_average_estimate.png/520px-Romani_population_average_estimate.png 2x" data-file-width="788" data-file-height="596" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Distribution of the Romani people in Europe (2007 <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> "average estimates", totalling 9.8 million)<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sap34.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Sap34.jpg/220px-Sap34.jpg" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Sap34.jpg/330px-Sap34.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Sap34.jpg/440px-Sap34.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3015" data-file-height="2530" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sap34.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Antiziganist protests in <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>, 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Modern_Antiziganism" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Antiziganism">Modern Antiziganism</a></div>
<p>In Europe, Romani people are associated with poverty, are accused of high rates of crime and behaviours that are perceived by the rest of the population as being antisocial or inappropriate.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> Partly for this reason, discrimination against the Romani people has continued to the present day,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup> although efforts are being made to address them.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> reports continued instances of <a href="/wiki/Antiziganism" title="Antiziganism">Antizigan</a> discrimination during the 20th Century, particularly in Romania, Serbia,<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[220]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[221]</a></sup> The European Union has recognized that discrimination against Romani must be addressed, and with the national Roma integration strategy they encourage member states to work towards greater Romani inclusion and upholding the <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_the_Roma_in_the_European_Union" title="Rights of the Roma in the European Union">rights of the Romani in the European union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup></p>
<div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"><small>*projections for Serbia also include up to 97.000 <a href="/wiki/IDPs" class="mw-redirect" title="IDPs">Roma IDPs</a> in Serbia<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup></small>

<p>The Romanis of Kosovo have been severely persecuted by ethnic Albanians since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, and the region's Romani community is, for the most part, annihilated.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>Czechoslovakia carried out a policy of sterilization of Romani women, starting in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup> The dissidents of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_77" title="Charter 77">Charter 77</a> denounced it in 1977–78 as a <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>, but the practice continued through the <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a> of 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> A 2005 report by the Czech government's independent ombudsman, Otakar Motejl, identified dozens of cases of coercive sterilization between 1979 and 2001, and called for criminal investigations and possible prosecution against several health care workers and administrators.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, following the brutal rape and subsequent murder of an Italian woman in Rome at the hands of a young man from a local Romani encampment,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup> the Italian government declared that Italy's Romani population represented a national security risk and that swift action was required to address the <i>emergenza nomadi</i> (<i>nomad emergency</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup> Specifically, officials in the Italian government accused the Romanies of being responsible for rising crime rates in urban areas.</p>
<p>The 2008 <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Cristina_and_Violetta_Djeordsevic" title="Death of Cristina and Violetta Djeordsevic">deaths of Cristina and Violetta Djeordsevic</a>, two Roma children who drowned while Italian beach-goers remained unperturbed, brought international attention to the relationship between Italians and the Roma people. Reviewing the state of play in 2012, one Belgian magazine observed:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>On International Roma Day, which falls on 8 April, the significant proportion of Europe's 12 million Roma who live in deplorable conditions will not have much to celebrate. And poverty is not the only worry for the community. Ethnic tensions are on the rise. In 2008, Roma camps came under attack in Italy, intimidation by racist parliamentarians is the norm in Hungary. Speaking in 1993, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel" title="Václav Havel">Václav Havel</a> prophetically remarked that "the treatment of the Roma is a litmus test for democracy": and democracy has been found wanting. The consequences of the transition to capitalism have been disastrous for the Roma. Under communism they had jobs, free housing and schooling. Now many are unemployed, many are losing their homes and racism is increasingly rewarded with impunity.<sup id="cite_ref-MO_2012_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MO_2012-232">[231]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forced_repatriation">Forced repatriation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Forced repatriation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Romani_people_from_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Expulsion of Romani people from France">Expulsion of Romani people from France</a></div>
<p>In the summer of 2010 French authorities demolished at least 51 illegal Roma camps and began the <a href="/wiki/French_Romani_repatriation" class="mw-redirect" title="French Romani repatriation">process of repatriating</a> their residents to their countries of origin.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup> This followed tensions between the French state and Roma communities, which had been heightened after French police opened fire and killed a traveller who drove through a police checkpoint, hitting an officer, and attempted to hit two more officers at another checkpoint. In retaliation a group of Roma, armed with hatchets and iron bars, attacked the police station of Saint-Aignan, toppled traffic lights and road signs and burned three cars.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup> The French government has been accused of perpetrating these actions to pursue its political agenda.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup> EU Justice Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Viviane_Reding" title="Viviane Reding">Viviane Reding</a> stated that the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> should take legal action against France over the issue, calling the deportations "a disgrace". Purportedly, a leaked file dated 5 August, sent from the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Interior_(France)" title="Minister of the Interior (France)">Interior Ministry</a> to regional police chiefs included the instruction: "Three hundred camps or illegal settlements must be cleared within three months, Roma camps are a priority."<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fictional_representations">Fictional representations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Fictional representations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_fiction" title="Romani people in fiction">Romani people in fiction</a></div>
<p>Many fictional depictions of Romani people in literature and art present romanticized narratives of their supposed mystical powers of <a href="/wiki/Fortune_telling" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortune telling">fortune telling</a> or their supposed irascible or passionate temper paired with an indomitable love of freedom and a habit of criminality. Particularly notable are classics like the story <i><a href="/wiki/Carmen_(novella)" title="Carmen (novella)">Carmen</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Prosper_M%C3%A9rim%C3%A9e" title="Prosper Mérimée">Prosper Mérimée</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Carmen" title="Carmen">opera based on it</a> by <a href="/wiki/Georges_Bizet" title="Georges Bizet">Georges Bizet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugo" title="Victor Hugo">Victor Hugo</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunchback_of_Notre_Dame" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hunchback of Notre Dame">The Hunchback of Notre Dame</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Herge" class="mw-redirect" title="Herge">Herge</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Castafiore_Emerald" title="The Castafiore Emerald">The Castafiore Emerald</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">Miguel de Cervantes</a>' <i>La Gitanilla</i>. The Romani were also depicted in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Midsummer_Night%27s_Dream" title="A Midsummer Night's Dream">A Midsummer Night's Dream</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/As_You_Like_It" title="As You Like It">As You Like It</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Othello" title="Othello">Othello</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tempest" title="The Tempest">The Tempest</a></i>, all by <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>.</p>
<p>The Romani were also heavily romanticized in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, a classic example being the 1975 <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_of_the_Gypsies" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of the Gypsies">Tabor ukhodit v Nebo</a></i>. A more realistic depiction of contemporary <a href="/wiki/Romani_in_the_Balkans" class="mw-redirect" title="Romani in the Balkans">Romani in the Balkans</a>, featuring Romani lay actors speaking in their native dialects, although still playing with established clichés of a Romani penchant for both magic and crime, was presented by <a href="/wiki/Emir_Kusturica" title="Emir Kusturica">Emir Kusturica</a> in his <i><a href="/wiki/Time_of_the_Gypsies" title="Time of the Gypsies">Time of the Gypsies</a></i> (1988) and <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Cat,_White_Cat" title="Black Cat, White Cat">Black Cat, White Cat</a></i> (1998). The films of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Gatlif" title="Tony Gatlif">Tony Gatlif</a>, a French director of Romani ethnicity, like <i>Les Princes</i> (1983), <i><a href="/wiki/Latcho_Drom" title="Latcho Drom">Latcho Drom</a></i> (1993) and <i>Gadjo Dilo</i> (1997) also portray gypsy life.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romani_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-212"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-212">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Most estimates for numbers of Romani victims of the Holocaust fall between 200,000 and 500,000, although figures ranging between 90,000 and 4 million have been proposed. Lower estimates do not include those killed in all Axis-controlled countries. A detailed study by Sybil Milton, formerly senior historian at the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Holocaust_Memorial_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Holocaust Memorial Museum">U.S. Holocaust Memorial Museum</a> gave a figure of at least a minimum of 220,000, probably higher, possibly closer to 500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> Ian Hancock, Director of the Program of Romani Studies and the Romani Archives and Documentation Center at the University of Texas at Austin, argues in favour of a higher figure of between 500,000 and 1,500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2016-07-27</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARomani+people&amp;rft.atitle=Diagn%C3%83%B3stico+social+de+la+comunidad+gitana+en+Espa%C3%83%B1a&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.msc.es%2Fssi%2FfamiliasInfancia%2FinclusionSocial%2FpoblacionGitana%2Fdocs%2Fdiagnosticosocial_autores.pdf&amp;rft.jtitle=Msc.es&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/2011_Romanian_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Romanian Census">2011 census</a> data, based on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.recensamantromania.ro/rezultate-2/">table 7 Population by ethnicity</a>, gives a total of 621,573 Roma in Romania. This figure is disputed by other sources, because at the local level, many Roma declare a different ethnicity (mostly Romanian, but also Hungarian in Transylvania and Turkish in Dobruja). Many are not recorded at all, since they do not have ID cards <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.edrc.ro/docs/docs/Romii_din_Romania.pdf">[2]</a>. International sources give higher figures than the official census(<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://europeandcis.undp.org/uploads/public/File/rbec_web/vgr/chapter1.1.pdf"></a><a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>'s Regional Bureau for Europe, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.worldbank.org/WBSITE/EXTERNAL/COUNTRIES/ECAEXT/EXTROMA/0,,contentMDK:20333806~menuPK:615999~pagePK:64168445~piPK:64168309~theSitePK:615987,00.html">World Bank</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.msd.govt.nz/documents/publications/msd/journal/issue25/25-pages154-164.pdf">International Association for Official Statistics</a>).</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://romani.humanities.manchester.ac.uk/downloads/2/Matras_Rmni_ELL.pdf">"Romani"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. <i>Encyclopedia of Language and Linguistics</i>. Oxford: Elsevier. p.&#160;1<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2009-08-30</span></span>. <q>In some regions of Europe, especially the western margins (Britain, the Iberian peninsula), Romani-speaking communities have given up their language in favor of the majority language, but have retained Romani-derived vocabulary as an in-group code. <li><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lety-memorial.cz/history_en.aspx"><i>History</i></a>, CZ: Lety memorial</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARomani+people&amp;rft.btitle=History&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lety-memorial.cz%2Fhistory_en.aspx&amp;rft.place=CZ&amp;rft.pub=Lety+memorial&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>.</li>
<li><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.europarl.eu.int/omk/sipade3?SAME_LEVEL=1&amp;LEVEL=5&amp;NAV=X&amp;DETAIL=&amp;PUBREF=-//EP//TEXT+TA+P6-TA-2005-0151+0+DOC+XML+V0//EN"><i>The situation of the Roma in the European Union</i></a> (resolution), European Parliament, April 28, 2005</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARomani+people&amp;rft.btitle=The+situation+of+the+Roma+in+the+European+Union&amp;rft.date=2005-04-28&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.europarl.eu.int%2Fomk%2Fsipade3%3FSAME_LEVEL%3D1%26LEVEL%3D5%26NAV%3DX%26DETAIL%3D%26PUBREF%3D-%2F%2FEP%2F%2FTEXT%2BTA%2BP6-TA-2005-0151%2B0%2BDOC%2BXML%2BV0%2F%2FEN&amp;rft.pub=European+Parliament&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>.</li>
<li><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wcd.coe.int/ViewDoc.jsp?id=962605&amp;Site=COE"><i>Final report on the human rights situation of the Roma, Sinti and travellers in Europe</i></a>, The European Commissioner for <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">Human Rights</a> (<a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>), February 15, 2006</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARomani+people&amp;rft.btitle=Final+report+on+the+human+rights+situation+of+the+Roma%2C+Sinti+and+travellers+in+Europe&amp;rft.date=2006-02-15&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwcd.coe.int%2FViewDoc.jsp%3Fid%3D962605%26Site%3DCOE&amp;rft.pub=The+European+Commissioner+for+Human+Rights+%28Council+of+Europe%29&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>.</li>
<li>Shot in remote areas of the Thar desert in Northwest India, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Zirn1H4vE0Y"><span class="plainlinks">Jaisalmer Ayo: Gateway of the Gypsies</span></a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> captures the lives of vanishing nomadic communities who are believed to share common ancestors with the Roma people&#160;–  released 2004</li>
</ul>
